25:T5f43,<entryFree id="n36773" key="كَذَبَ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <itype>1</itype>        
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">كَذَبَ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, aor.      
    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Bi" lang="ar">كَذِبَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">كَذِبٌ</foreign> (a strange form of inf. n.; there being, accord. to Kz., only fourteen instances of it; as <foreign lang="ar">لَعِبٌ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">ضَحِكٌ</foreign>, &amp;c.; though there are many substantives of this measure; MF) and <foreign lang="ar">كِذْبٌ</foreign> (S, K: accord. to Ibn-Es-Seed and others, this latter is formed from the former, by putting the second vowel of the former in the place of the first: MF) and <foreign lang="ar">كَذِبَةٌ</foreign> (L) or <foreign lang="ar">كَذْبَةٌ</foreign> (K) and <foreign lang="ar">كِذْبَهٌ</foreign> (L, K) and <foreign lang="ar">كِذَابٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">كِذَّابٌ</foreign> (K: but this last, which is also assigned to <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ</foreign> in the L, is, accord. to the S, which refers, for proof, to the Kur, ch. lxxviii. 28, one of the inf. ns. of <foreign lang="ar">كذّب</foreign>: and Ks says, that the people of El-Yemen make the inf. n. of <foreign lang="ar">فعّل</foreign> of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فِعَّالٌ</foreign>, while the other Arabs make it <foreign lang="ar">تَفْعِيلٌ</foreign>: TA) and, accord. to some, <foreign lang="ar">كُذْبٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">كَذْبٌ</foreign> (TA: but the latter of these two, though agreeable with analogy, is unheard: TA): see also <foreign lang="ar">كَذِبٌ</foreign>, below: [<hi rend="ital">He lied; uttered a falsehood; said what was untrue:</hi>] <hi rend="ital">he gave an untrue account,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">relation, of a thing, whether intentionally</hi> or <hi rend="ital">unintentionally.</hi> (Msb) <foreign lang="ar">الكَذِبُ</foreign> is of five kinds.          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  First, <hi rend="ital">The relater's changing,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">altering, what he hears; and his relating; as</hi> 
                  <pb n="2598"/> 
                  <hi rend="ital">from others, what he does not know.</hi> This is the kind that renders one criminal, and destroys manly virtue. — Second, <hi rend="ital">The saying what resembles a lie, not meaning anything but the truth.</hi> Such is meant in the trad., <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ إِبْرٰهِيمُ ثَلَاثَ كَذِبَاتٍ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Abraham said three sayings resembling lies;</hi> he being veracious in the three. — Third, <hi rend="ital">The saying what is untrue by mistake,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">unintentionally; making a mistake; erring.</hi> This signification is frequent. — Fourth, <hi rend="ital">The finding one's hopes false,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">vain.</hi> — Fifth, <hi rend="ital">The act of instigating,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">inciting.</hi> (IAmb.) [See illustrations of these and other significations below; and see more <hi rend="ital">voce</hi> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">صَدَقَ</foreign>.] [You say] <foreign lang="ar">يَكْذِبُكَ مِنْ أَيْنَ جَاءَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He will lie to thee</hi> even <hi rend="ital">as to the place whence he comes.</hi>] (L, art. <foreign lang="ar">مح</foreign>, and in many other places, following the similar phrase <foreign lang="ar">لَا يَصْدُقُكَ أَثَرَهُ</foreign>, or <foreign lang="ar">أَثَرُهُ</foreign>.) Lebeed says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">اِكْذِبِ النَّفْسَ إِذَا حَدَّثْتَهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Lie to the soul</hi> (i. e., <hi rend="ital">to thy soul,</hi>) <hi rend="ital">when thou talkest to it:</hi> i. e., say not to thy soul, Thou wilt not succeed in thine enterprise; for thy doing so will divert thee, or hinder thee, therefrom. A proverb. (Meyd, &amp;c.)          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">كُذِبَ</foreign>, pass., <hi rend="ital">He was told a lie; a falsehood;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an untruth.</hi> (K.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  Aboo-Duwád says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ العَيْرُ وَإِنْ كَانَ بَرَحْ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> 
                  <hi rend="ital">The wild ass hath lied, although he hath passed from right to left:</hi> [the doing which is esteemed unlucky:] or, [agreeably with explanations of <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ</foreign> given below,] <hi rend="ital">hath become languid, and within</hi> [<hi rend="ital">the sportsman's</hi>] <hi rend="ital">power,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">reach, &amp;c.:</hi> or <hi rend="ital">keep to the wild ass, and hunt him, &amp;c.</hi> A proverb, applied in the case of a thing that is hoped for, though difficult of attainment. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَتْ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36773-1" target="كذّبت" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n36773"/></foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">She</hi> (a camel), <hi rend="ital">being covered by the stallion, raised her tail, and then returned without conceiving.</hi> (En-Nadr, K.)          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ</foreign> is said of other things than men [and animals]: as of lightning, [meaning <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">It gave a false promise of rain</hi>]: of a dream, an opinion, a hope, and a desire, [meaning, in each of these cases, <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">It proved false</hi>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="7">-b7-</sense>  So also <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَتِ العَيْنُ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The sense</hi> [i. e., <hi rend="ital">the sight</hi>] <hi rend="ital">of the eye deceived it.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="8">-b8-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ الرَّأْىُ</foreign> [<assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">The judgment lied</hi>]; i. e., <hi rend="ital">he imagined the thing contrary to its real state.</hi> (TA.) [See also <foreign lang="ar">صَدَقَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">ظَنِّى</foreign>]          <sense type="b" n="9">-b9-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَتْكَ عَيْنُكَ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">Thine eye showed thee what had no reality.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="10">-b10-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ لَبَنُ النَّاقَةِ</foreign>, and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36773-2" target="كذّب" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n36773"/></foreign>, (the latter mentioned in the S,) <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">The milk of the camel passed away,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">failed.</hi> (Lh.)          <sense type="b" n="11">-b11-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ فِى سَيْرِهِ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  [<hi rend="ital">He</hi> (a camel) <hi rend="ital">became slack,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">slow, in his pace:</hi> see 2]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="12">-b12-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ الحَرُّ</foreign> <tropical>(tropical:)</tropical>  <hi rend="ital">The heat abated.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="13">-b13-</sense>  See also 2. <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He found his hopes to be false,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">vain.</hi> (IAmb.) <foreign lang="ar">اُنْظُرْ كَيْفَ كَذَبُوا عَلَى</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَنْفُسِهِمْ</foreign>, [Kur vi. 24, lit., <hi rend="ital">See how they lied against themselves,</hi>] is said to signify <hi rend="ital">see how their hope hath proved false,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">vain.</hi> (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="14">-b14-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">ظَنُّوا أَنَّهُمْ قَدْ كُذِبُوا</foreign>, [Kur xii. 110,] <hi rend="ital">They</hi> (the apostles) <hi rend="ital">thought that they had been disappointed of the fulfilment of the promise made to them.</hi> So accord. to one reading. Accord. to another reading, the verb is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36773-3" target="كُذِّبُوا" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>: [in which case, the meaning of the words appears to be, “ They knew that they had been pronounced liars ” by the people to whom they were sent]. (TA.) There are also two other readings;   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n36773-4" target="كَذَّبُوا" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبُوا</foreign>: accord. to the former, the verb refers to the people to whom the apostles were sent; and <foreign lang="ar">ظنّوا</foreign> means “ they knew: ” accord. to the latter, the words mean, “ They (the people above mentioned) thought that they (the apostles) had broken their promise. ” (Jel.)          <sense type="b" n="15">-b15-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">مَا كَذَبَ الفُؤَادُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مَا رَأَى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The mind did not belie what he saw.</hi>] (Kur liii. 11.)          <sense type="b" n="16">-b16-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَتْهُ نَفْسُهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">His soul lied to him:</hi>] <hi rend="ital">his soul made him to desire things, and to conceive hopes, that could scarcely come to pass.</hi> (K.) Hence the soul is called <foreign lang="ar">الكَذُوبُ</foreign>. You say in the contr. case, <foreign lang="ar">صَذَقَتْهُ نفسه</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">الكَذُوبُ</foreign>. (TA.) See <foreign lang="ar">كَذُوبٌ</foreign>, and art. <foreign lang="ar">صدق</foreign>.          <sense type="b" n="17">-b17-</sense>  Hence, <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ عَلَيْهِ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">It rendered him active,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">brisk; animated him; instigated him; incited him;</hi> (K;) as also <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَهُ</foreign>. (Z.)          <sense type="b" n="18">-b18-</sense>  Hence, <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَكَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ عَلَيْكَ</foreign> have sometimes the same signification, though not always the same government, as <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكَ</foreign>, or <foreign lang="ar">اِلْزَمْ</foreign>; <hi rend="ital">Keep to;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">take to.</hi> The noun following is put in the nom. case accord. to the dial. of El-Yemen; and in the acc. accord. to the dial. of Mudar; or, as some say, is correctly put in the nom. only. (TA.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ عَلَيْكَ كَذَا وَكَذَا</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Keep to,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">take to, such and such things.</hi> It is an extr. phrase. (ISk.) You also say, <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبْتُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكَ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Keep thou to me:</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">كذبتُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكُمْ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">Keep ye to me.</hi> IAar. cites the following verse of Khidásh Ibn-Zuheyr, [in which he tauntingly compares a people to ticks]: <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبْتُ عَلَيْكُمْ أَوْ عِدُونِى وَعَلِّلُوا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">بِىَ الأَرْضَ وَالأَقْوَامَ قِرْدَانَ مَوْظَبَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Keep ye to me: threaten me, and soothe by</hi> (<hi rend="ital">the mention of</hi>) <hi rend="ital">me the land and the peoples, O ticks of Mowdhab!</hi>]: meaning Keep ye to me, and to satirizing me, when ye are on a journey, and traverse the land mentioning me. (TA.) In like manner, <foreign lang="ar">يَوْمُ الأَحَدِ والخَمِيسِ كَذَبَاكَ أَوْ يَوْمُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">الإِثْنَيْنِ والثَّلَاثَاءِ</foreign>, in a trad. respecting the proper days for being cupped, signifies <hi rend="ital">Keep thou to Sunday and Thursday,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">Monday and Tuesday.</hi> (IAth, Z.) The verb is thus used after the manner of a proverb, and is invariable [as to tense], being constantly in the pret. tense, connected [literally or virtually, when explained by <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكَ</foreign> followed by the prep. <foreign lang="ar">ب</foreign>, or by <foreign lang="ar">إِلْزَمْ</foreign>,] only with the person addressed, and in the sense of the imperative. <foreign lang="ar">كذباك</foreign> here [lit.] signifies <hi rend="ital">Let</hi> them <hi rend="ital">render thee active,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">brisk, and animate thee, instigate thee,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">incite thee.</hi> (Z.). [A trad. of 'Omar, quoted below, presents another instance to which this signification is said to apply.]          <sense type="b" n="19">-b19-</sense>  Or <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ</foreign> denotes instigation, or incitement, of the person addressed, to keep to the thing that is mentioned; as in the saying of the Arabs, <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ عَلَيْكَ العَسَلُ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">Eat thou honey:</hi> but the explanation of this is, (<hi rend="ital">The relinquisher of</hi>) <hi rend="ital">honey hath erred</hi> [<hi rend="ital">to thee;</hi> i. e., in his representation of its evil qualites &amp;c.; which is equivalent to saying, <hi rend="ital">Eat,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">keep to, honey</hi>]: <foreign lang="ar">العَسَلُ</foreign> being put for <foreign lang="ar">تَارِكُ العَسَلِ</foreign>. [See also 1 in art. <foreign lang="ar">عسل</foreign>.] In like manner, the saying of 'Omar, <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الحَجُّ</foreign> &amp;c., (see below,) signifies <hi rend="ital">Keep ye to the performance of the pilgrimage, &amp;c.:</hi> [or (<hi rend="ital">the relinquisher of</hi>) <hi rend="ital">the pilgrimage hath erred to thee</hi> in his representation of it: therefore it means as above]. (IAmb.) Accord. to IAmb the noun signifying the object of instigation [which may also be called the cause thereof] cannot be rightly put in the acc. case: if so put, the verb is without an agent. (TA.) [But see what is said on this point in the remarks on the trad. of 'Omar below.]          <sense type="b" n="20">-b20-</sense>  Or the verb in a case of this kind signifies <foreign lang="ar">أَمْكَنَ</foreign>: thus, <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَكَ الحَجُّ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">The performance of the pilgrimage is possible,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">practicable, to thee:</hi> therefore [it means] <hi rend="ital">Perform thou the pilgrimage.</hi> (ISh.)          <sense type="b" n="21">-b21-</sense>  Or <foreign lang="ar">أَمْكَنَ</foreign> is its original signification; and the meaning intended is <hi rend="ital">Keep to;</hi> as in the ex. <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ العَتِيقُ</foreign>. (Aal.)          <sense type="b" n="22">-b22-</sense>  'Antarah, addressing his wife 'Ableh, says; or, accord. to some, the poet is Khuzaz Ibn-Lowdhán; <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ العَتِيقُ وَمَآءُ شَنٍّ بَارِدٌ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">إِنْ كُنْتِ سَائِلَتِى غَبُوقًا فَٱذْهَبِى</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> (TA.) i. e., <hi rend="ital">Keep thou to</hi> the eating of <hi rend="ital">dates, and to the cool water of an old, worn-out, skin: if thou ask me for an evening's drink of milk, depart:</hi> for I have appropriated the milk to my colt, which is profitable to me, and may preserve me and thee: (L:) <foreign lang="ar">العتيق</foreign> is in the nom. case accord. to the dial. of El-Yemen: but in the acc. accord. to that of Mudar. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="23">-b23-</sense>  Er-Radee [reading <foreign lang="ar">العتيقَ</foreign>] cites this verse as a proof that <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ</foreign>, originally a verb, has become a verbal noun, signifying <foreign lang="ar">اِلْزَمْ</foreign>. (TA.) But he is the only one who asserts it to be a verbal noun. (MF.)          <sense type="b" n="24">-b24-</sense>  Also, Mo'akkir El-Bárikee says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">وَذُبْيَانِيَّةٍ أُوْصَتْ بَنِيهَا</foreign>
                     </L> 
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">بِأَنْ كَذَبَ القَرَاطِفُ وَالقُرُوفُ</foreign>
                     </L> 
                  </quote> 
                  <hi rend="ital">And many a woman of Dhubyán charged her sons by</hi> [<hi rend="ital">saying</hi>], <hi rend="ital">Keep to the red garments</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">اكسية</foreign>), <hi rend="ital">and the bags</hi> (or <hi rend="ital">receptacles</hi>) <hi rend="ital">of leather tanned with pomegranate-bark.</hi> She charged them to take plenty of these two things as spoil from the tribe of Nemir, if they should prevail over them. (Aboo-'Obeyd El-Kásim Ibn-Selám.)          <sense type="b" n="25">-b25-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">كذب</foreign> is also said to have the same <pb n="2599"/> meaning in the words of the trad. <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ النَّسَّابُونَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Keep to those skilled in genealogy:</hi>] or <hi rend="ital">Regard is to be had to what is said by those skilled in genealogy:</hi> another meaning to which is assigned below. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="26">-b26-</sense>  It sometimes signifies <hi rend="ital">It is incumbent,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">obligatory.</hi> So in the following: (a trad. of 'Omar: TA:) <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الحَجُّ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ عَلَيْكُمُ العُمْرَةُ كَذَبَ عَلَيْكُمُ الجِهَادُ ثلَاثَةُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَسْفَارٍ كَذَبْنَ عَلَيْكُمْ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">The performance of the pilgrimage is incumbent on you: the performance of</hi> (<hi rend="ital">the rites called</hi>) <foreign lang="ar">العمرة</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">is incumbent on you: warring</hi> (<hi rend="ital">for the sake of religion</hi>) <hi rend="ital">is incumbent on you: three expeditions are incumbent on you</hi>]: (S, * K:) or <foreign lang="ar">كذب</foreign>, here, is from <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَتْهُ نَفْسُهُ</foreign>, “ his soul made him to desire things, and to conceive hopes, that could scarcely come to pass; ” and the meaning is <hi rend="ital">let</hi> [<hi rend="ital">the expectation of the reward which will follow</hi>] <hi rend="ital">the performance of the pilgrimage render thee active,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">brisk, and animate thee, instigate thee,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">incite thee, to the act:</hi> [and so of the rest of the trad.: but here I should observe, that, for <foreign lang="ar">لِيَكْذِبَكَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">لِيُنَشِّطَكَ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">يَبْعَثَكَ</foreign>, in the CK, we should read <foreign lang="ar">لِيَكْذِبْكَ</foreign> &amp;c.:] (K:)          <sense type="b" n="27">-b27-</sense>  or, as ISk says, <foreign lang="ar">كذب</foreign>, here, seems to denote instigation, or incitement, meaning <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكُمْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">بِهِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">keep ye to it;</hi> and is an extr. word with respect to analogy: (S:)          <sense type="b" n="28">-b28-</sense>  accord. to Akh., <foreign lang="ar">الحجّ</foreign> is governed in the nom. case by <foreign lang="ar">كذب</foreign>; but as to the meaning, it is in the acc.; because the meaning is a command to perform the pilgrimage; as when you say, <foreign lang="ar">أَمْكَنَكَ الصَّيْدُ</foreign> [“ the game hath become within thy power, or reach ”], meaning “ shoot it, ” or “ cast at it: ” (S:) he who puts <foreign lang="ar">الحجّ</foreign> in the acc. case, [agreeably with one relation of the trad., TA,] makes <foreign lang="ar">عليك</foreign> [or <foreign lang="ar">عليكم</foreign>] a verbal noun; and in <foreign lang="ar">كذب</foreign> is [implied] the pronoun which refers to <foreign lang="ar">الحجّ</foreign> [and which is the agent of the verb]; (K;) or the agent is implied in <foreign lang="ar">كذب</foreign>, and explained by what follows it; (Sb;) [so that] the meaning is <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ الحَجُّ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">عَلَيْكُمُ الحَجَّ</foreign>: (Z:) or, [as shown above,] <foreign lang="ar">كذب</foreign> is a verbal n., meaning <foreign lang="ar">الْزَمْ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">الحجّ</foreign> is in the acc. case as governed by it: (Er-Radee:) though its being in the acc. case, accord. to some, is altogether unknown: (TA:)          <sense type="b" n="29">-b29-</sense>  [or the meaning is as stated before on the authority of ISh.:]          <sense type="b" n="30">-b30-</sense>  or the trad. means <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ عَلَيْكَ الحَجُّ إِنْ ذُكِرَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَنَّهُ غَيْرُ كَافٍ هَادِمٍ لِمَا قَبْلَهُ مِنَ الذُّنُوبِ</foreign> [(<hi rend="ital">the relinguisher of</hi>) <hi rend="ital">the pilgrimage hath erred to thee</hi> if it have been spoken of (by him) as not sufficient, (and as not) abolishing the sins, or offences, (committed) before it: agreeably with the explanation by IAmb, given above]. (K.)          <sense type="b" n="31">-b31-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">He said what was false unintentionally; committed a mistake,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">error.</hi> The verb is used in this sense by the people of El-Hijáz, and the rest of the Arabs have followed them in so using it. (Towsheeh.)       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ</foreign> is also said to signify <hi rend="ital">He spoke truth;</hi> so as to bear two contr. meanings: and thus, <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَ النَّسَّابُونَ</foreign> may signify <hi rend="ital">Those skilled in genealogy have spoken truth:</hi> but another explanation of this saying is given in this art. (MF, &amp;c.)       <sense type="A" n="3">-A3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">كَذَبَتْ عَفَّاقَتُكَ</foreign> [and the like] <hi rend="ital">Thou brokest wind.</hi> (S in art. <foreign lang="ar">عفق</foreign>.)    </entryFree>26:T1629,<entryFree id="n36774" key="كذّبه" type="main">

                  <hi rend="ital">He found him a liar; an utterer of falsehood;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a sayer of what was untrue:</hi> (S, K:) or <hi rend="ital">he said to him,</hi> “ <hi rend="ital">Thou hast lied</hi> ”: <hi rend="ital">&amp;c.:</hi> (TA:) or this verb bears the former of these two significations, and
